B005DKLPF6|5.0|The fifth opus from Atlanta prog/doom metallers Mastodon differs quite greatly from their last, 2009's \\"Crack The Skye.\\" For starters, it is a significantly heavier and more viscerally-satisfying affair. Brent Hinds and Bill Kelliher's massive avalanches of excellent, downtuned, Sabbath-y riffage, and Brann Dailor's bullying, Melvins-esque drumming see to this. Furthermore, 2011's \\"The Hunter\\" is a lot more concise and compact. Indeed, although their arrangements are no less complex or technical, the songwriting has altered this time around, as Mastodon now seem content to just kick out the jams (motha!), trimming down excessive progressive wankery, superfluous fat, and/or ornamental flourishes. The songs' playing times have been trimmed down significantly, too. Whereas \\"Skye\\" had only one track under five-minutes long (and two that were well-over ten-minutes), there are only two tracks, here, that crack the five-minute barrier. All told, \\"The Hunter\\" actually has more in common with 2002's major-length debut, \\"Remission,\\" but even those two are two very different albums. Come to think of it, none of this quartet's records are the exact same. (Hence, if nothing else, they at least deserve credit for never releasing a set of songs that is a simple rehash of any of their previous works.)<br /><br />The ball gets rolling quickly and steadily with \\"Black One,\\" a track that almost sounds as if it could be a b-side from the \\"Leviathan\\" recording sessions. Its thunderous rhythms are comprised of crunching, grumbling bass grooves, jazzy, polyrhythmic drum slamming, and towering sludge metal riffs. But no matter how good this opener is, it is almost (almost, but not quite) overshadowed by its successor, \\"Curl Of The Burl.\\" An abundance of soaring, skyscraper guitar harmonies, instantly memorable choruses, and infectious \\"ooh\\" sing-along refrains make it quite possibly the catchiest and most commercially-accessible (read: hit-single-worthy) tune in the Mastodon playbook to date!<br /><br />\\"Blasteroid\\" again dives back into the muck with sludgy guitar licks and busy, pummeling, rapid-fire drumming. \\"Stargasm\\" continues to stomp you under foot, storming forward with thundering, Southern sludge-filled grooves, grinding, lumbering rhythms, and ultra-hefty bass bottom. Some more epic melodic choruses -- that are soaring and have stadium-sized vocals that are clean without descending into emo-territory -- are blended into the mix, here, though, too. Similarly, the hilariously-named \\"Octopus Has No Friends\\" also has instinctively memorable, cleanly-sung choruses to go along with its usual abundance of ominous doom riffs, beeping, grumbling -- and, at times, almost funky-sounding -- bass lines, and superbly dexterous drumming. And so does \\"All The Heavy Lifting,\\" which features another terrifically catchy and epic chorus that will be bouncing around your head for days. Oh, and how about the tune's crunchy, chunked-up riffing and rolling bass groove, are simply icing on the cake.<br /><br />The album's second half takes on a concertedly more progressive approach, with cuts like the dreamy title track entering the fray. It is an acoustic ballad with shredding, unorthodoxly bluesy soloing, supple crooning, and screaming guitar harmonies. It is also the first epic on the record to be over five-minutes in length. But there is still plenty of heavy stuff to be had, here, too, as \\"Dry Bone Valley,\\" which is a very brisk and bludgeoning number backed by thrashy, fiery, buzzsaw picking and punishing blast beat-esque thudding, proves nicely. And the whammy bar-soaked solo that comes ripping through the mix is simply icing on the cake. \\"Thickening\\" works likewise, fading-in with a melodic guitar and bass intro before suddenly, dramatically flying in the opposite direction, as huge, ultra-tasty, chug and churn guitars (which evoke \\"Sabbath Bloody Sabbath\\" very closely, by the way) come storming in. A handful of other fairly dazzling solo flights are included, too.<br /><br />Then things briefly go back into experimental territory again, as the listener is dealt a sudden, dramatic curveball in the form of \\"Creature Lives.\\" It has a really trippy, new wave-y intro that would not be out of placed coming off of a Skinny Puppy or KMFDM outing, followed by miles of deliciously melodic guitar and bass work (including tons of stunning, jazzy guitar soloing). And \\"The Hunter\\"'s final remaining piece of pure prog metal -- \\"The Sparrow,\\" a very Pink Floyd-ian, five-and-a-half-minute closing semi-ballad backed by an acoustic intro, harmonic, accompanying bass line, and totally air-guitar-able melodic solo -- comes soon thereafter. But not before the band drop two more absolutely brutal cuts: The merciless and booming \\"Spectrelight\\" and the machine gun drum-driven \\"Bedazzled Fingernals\\" (again, don't let song titles fool you; the music is 100% serious, I swear!).<br /><br />Stripping this review of its fat, Georgia's finest metal collective couldn't suck even if they tried to. This excellent record is but one more piece of evidence of how very true that fact is. It should please all fans of the band and the sludge/doom and progressive metal genres. Plus, if you're new to Mastodon, you could do a lot worse than to start right here, too. So, yeah...definitely \\"Hunt\\" this album down.ded, too.<br /><br />Then things briefly go back into experimental territory again, as the listener is dealt a sudden, dramatic curveball in the form of \\"Creature Lives.\\" It has a really trippy, new wave-y intro that would not be out of placed coming off of a Skinny Puppy or KMFDM outing, followed by miles of deliciously melodic guitar and bass work (including tons of stunning, jazzy guitar soloing). And \\"The Hunter\\"'s final remaining piece of pure prog metal -- \\"The Sparrow,\\" a very Pink Floyd-ian, five-and-a-half-minute closing semi-ballad backed by an acoustic intro, harmonic, accompanying bass line, and totally air-guitar-able melodic solo -- comes soon thereafter. But not before the band drop two more absolutely brutal cuts: The merciless and booming \\"Spectrelight\\" and the machine gun drum-driven \\"Bedazzled Fingernals\\" (again, don't let song titles fool you; the music is 100% serious, I swear!).<br /><br />Stripping this review of its fat, Georgia's finest metal collective couldn't suck even if they tried to. This excellent record is but one more piece of evidence of how very true that fact is. It should please all fans of the band and the sludge/doom and progressive metal genres. Plus, if you're new to Mastodon, you could do a lot worse than to start right here, too. So, yeah...definitely \\"Hunt\\" this album down.

0345803493|2.0|I will admit, the first installment of Fifty Shades had me hooked. I think it was because Christian was so mysterious and Ana was so out of left field that the chemistry building between them kept me hanging on. I really thought the second installment would have done the same. Unfortunately, all I wanted to do was gauge my eyes out with a letter opener. I wanted to stop reading at Chapter 6 but I hung in there and finished the book. I was highly disappointed.<br /><br />First, the sex was over the top and quite repetitive. I really wish the author spaced the sex scenes every 5 chapters or 100 pages. Give us something to work our hormones up to. Alas, that didn't happen. Christian and Ana were having sex every few pages. I wound up skipping over every single sex scene between them. I was tired of reading about Ana biting her lip, Christian telling Ana how beautiful she was and Ana coming all around him. Ms James, could you use any other sexual phrases or detailing??<br /><br />Second, the characters got on my last nerve. From Ana's insecurities about not being enough for Christian and Christian begging Ana to never leave him, both characters are obviously made for each other. Oh, and how long is Ana going to dwell on Mrs Robinson (Who we later is Elena Lincoln and thinks Christian should be with her and not Ana)??? Seriously, ENOUGH! Christian must have told Ana that Mrs. R was in the past at least 20 times. It gets old!<br /><br />Third, what was the point of the scary, ex stalker sub, Leila, coming back into the picture? It gave the reader something to look forward to (a twist in the story, perhaps) but it was a complete fail. The only thing it did was cause a little bit of a stir and Ana witnessing the Dom/Sub power between Christian and Leila. This made Ana more insecure causing us to read about her insecurities for another 5-10 pages.<br /><br />Fourth, was there a plot other than Christian telling Ana he loved her and coming out with his demons/issues? If thatwas the plot, I'm sure it could have been written in under 250 pages and not drawn out to 500 pages. Too much \\"fluff\\" and unneeded nonsense.<br /><br />These books do not live up to the hype of the media. I can't believe they are considered best sellers.
